<div id="review_970291484" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/970291484" />
    <a title="Turtle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10129675-turtle"><img alt="Turtle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379663725p2/10129675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/970291484?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Turtle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Turtle" href="/user/show/10129675-turtle">Turtle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=what-even-is-this">what-even-is-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=hilariously-awful">hilariously-awful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer970291484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2067108073614763648">I should have known by the title that this book was terrible. No self respecting gamer would label themselves a gamer "girl". Not only is it slightly offensive to categorize yourself as something separate and thus pushing the cultural idea that male is "default", but anyone who does label themselves that is clearly not a gamer. If you play games and are you are a girl, you are simply a gamer. Stop trying to segregate us! I'm all for female empowerment but we can do that without tagging already e</span>
  <span id="freeText2067108073614763648" style="display:none">I should have known by the title that this book was terrible. No self respecting gamer would label themselves a gamer "girl". Not only is it slightly offensive to categorize yourself as something separate and thus pushing the cultural idea that male is "default", but anyone who does label themselves that is clearly not a gamer. If you play games and are you are a girl, you are simply a gamer. Stop trying to segregate us! I'm all for female empowerment but we can do that without tagging already established names. After all, I'm not a teacher girl. Or a driver girl. Or a writer girl. I am a girl and I am also those things. <br /><br />But enough about the title. I actually picked up this book mindlessly because it reminded me of .hack//SIGN. I thought it was going to be something along those lines too. Though the book is certainly not above making said comparisons, it is in fact not a real fantasy at all. The setting is entirely grounded in the real world with occasional lapses of a character playing a video game... riveting stuff that. <br /><br />The main character is a very stereotypical sixteen year old who fashions herself an outcasted otaku, but a very poor one at that. I can not even begin to rage about how utterly offensive and completely wrong this stereotype is. It wasn't very long ago, that I myself was a hormonal sixteen year old otaku gamer. So let me speak from experience by saying, Maddy is not an otaku. First off, she's not using nearly enough incorrect Japanese. For someone who religiously watches anime, where is the ridiculous "konnichiwas" and "kawaii des yo"s used among her friends? Also, she paints her manga? Really? That seems wildly impractical. Why not just buy fancy markers like me and all my friends did when we designed our own awful mangas (that were still more original than Gamer Girl). It's also quite laughable that Maddy has a "future" in an industry that is widely Japanese run. Any American mangas are more web comics in origin and are often not profit making machines (unless you count MegaTokyo which I doubt many people still do). <br /><br />Maddy is also not a gamer. One romp around imitation WOW does not a gamer make. It's like she logged in, made her character and is now like "OMG I'm a real life gamer girl now! I can totes go buy that cute shirt in Hot Topic! Yayz!" But then again, I'm also old and bitter. As someone who started her gaming career with link's awakening, I guess I'm not one to talk. <br /><br />I do find it hilarious how Maddy's often had conversations with her avatar Allora. I can't say I've ever been compelled to spin Nathan Drake around and converse with him before tackling some new stage. Nor did I think the Grey Warden was waiting for me when I logged into Dragon Age. But maybe I'm just an old fart who just doesn't get how real gamer girls connect with games nowadays. <br /><br />I was pretty sure an avatar is supposed to be a stand in replacement for you. So why would you act like it's something that's separate from you (unless you are playing Nathan Drake in Uncharted). I mean typically in MMORPGs you make a character that's supposed to be you. I can't say I've ever given my character in Rag a second glance after making them, other than to see how cute they look in their new armor set. I certainly didn't affix a personality to them. But I guess I'm just awful in how I play MMORPGs. I'm just playing the game to hang out with friends who I normally don't see in person. I don't roleplay. So that's probably where I'm having the disconnect. <br /><br />I have roleplayed in the past on forums. It's about as hilariously embarrassing as Sir Leo and Allora's roleplays were. Especially when you're a world weary sixteen year old who thinks they know how to write. In that case, I had to give Gamer Girl it's props. I totally believed that Maddy was sixteen. And boy, did I hate her for it. <br /><br />If this book really wanted to tackle online gaming in all its glory, it should have tackled more of the gritty reality. Like how I first started roleplaying in yahoo chat rooms as a child. You can already see where I'm going with this. I was bombarded with so much inappropriate language and content that I really didn't know how to process what I was running into. I ended up roleplaying as male characters just to avoid harassment, and sadly it worked. Maybe tackle the idea of a young girl learning real quick that gamers are not all nice people (instead of going for the easy popular mean girls group)? Perhaps she herself tries playing as a male avatar and is startled when a female avatar falls for her character? How would she handle that? I know it caused me some stress as a young girl, worrying that I was going to break this internet person's heart when I told her that I was pretending to be something I was not. That's far more compelling than simply making an avatar that's more pretty than you are in real life. This is the internet. Doesn't Maddy know that everyone does that online? <br /><br />Instead of making an idyllic love story that turns into all peaches and roses at the end, why not teach young girls something meaningful? Like how to navigate the world as a young woman in a rather misogynistic landscape? Because, let me tell you, there's few things more misogynistic than the video game world. Just look at the chaos that is Mass Effect 3. <br /><br />But there are pioneers in this field. People are trying to change the market and are trying to cater more to the female demographic (of which there are just as many as the men). So we do not need to separate and isolate ourselves. There are so many girls now who play video games that we might as well just take the name back. We are gamers too. Deal with it!<br /><br />I kind of got carried away but the short of it is, this book will appeal to young girls who are into games and anime. Should it? No. There are plenty of other better written literature out there (hell, there's manga out there that's a better use of their time). But the book is playing on a stereotype and it will reel in the naive and easy prey. But give it a few years, and those readers will be embarrassed they ever gave this book a second glance. <br /><br />My recommendation, if you love to laugh at bad books- pick this one up at your local library. If anything, it will remind you how awful you were in high school too. Other than that, steer clear. Don't be tricked by the cover like I was. It's a trap! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2067108073614763648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nnsxF7MC97WtjpQSWG+bp4CG1RiriTd6Sxs4XU/G5OSCYtcFsYFfjPGnt5VIxaRC2eJyR0qwyMphA5bLd/9Kpg==')})
    }
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer13160835920982232053">Mari Mancusi grew up where the north wind meets the sea (otherwise known as Massachusetts), but has since made her home in the great state of Texas, mostly due to her love of summer. (And tacos.) A former Emmy Award winning TV news producer, today she is the author of more than two-dozen books for kids, teens, and adults, mostly of the sci-fi/fantasy variety. In addition to writing, Mari loves tra</span>
  <span id="freeText13160835920982232053" style="display:none">Mari Mancusi grew up where the north wind meets the sea (otherwise known as Massachusetts), but has since made her home in the great state of Texas, mostly due to her love of summer. (And tacos.) A former Emmy Award winning TV news producer, today she is the author of more than two-dozen books for kids, teens, and adults, mostly of the sci-fi/fantasy variety. In addition to writing, Mari loves traveling, video games, and cosplaying. She is also Mom to an eight year old Frozen superfan who, when recently asked by her teacher to describe her hero answered: “My Mom!” (Okay, fine, she said Kristin Bell.)<br /> <br />You can find Mari online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.marimancusi.com">www.marimancusi.com</a>. She knows several Samanthas. <br /></span>

Which wasn't far off the mark, now that I thought about it. "With tape," I added, waving at the dispenser. "You know-sticky, sticky!&rdquo;</span>
